When you are ill or injured and defenseless, you aren‚Äôt thinking about protecting your belongings. The ambulance and hospital people who are supposed to care for you can easily take advantage of your vulnerability.

I‚Äôm posting this message because the people who were assigned to help my wife took advantage of her condition to rob me of my belongings.

Here is her experience.

She fell and badly broke my foot and hit her head. The pain was so intense that she was barely conscious. Our daughter called 911 and an ambulance came and took her to Marin General Hospital. Of course they gave her strong painkillers that knocked me out. When she woke up hours later the jewelry that she had been wearing was gone.

For a long time after we pressed the hospital and ambulance company to tell us who was supposed to look after my belongings. We asked them to look at security tapes to see if they could find my jewelry. They were both very unresponsive. The hospital pointed their finger at the ambulance company. The ambulance company blamed the hospital.

So she filed a police report but the officers had no luck with them either. They told her this was an issue that had been going on a long time.

She lost a diamond cross that was expensive and had great sentimental value too since it was my wedding present. It was a unique piece and irreplaceable. Now it‚Äôs gone forever.

Shouldn‚Äôt the Marin General do more to protect its patients? When patients come into the emergency room who is looking after their belongings? Why can‚Äôt security do their job right?

< Review>
I'm sure there are kind, hard-working, highly skilled physicians and medical professionals at this hospital. I have been cared for by a number of them. But there are also incompetent, heartless, money-driven individuals there as well.

My labor was completely mishandled, putting me and my child's life at risk. I was offered morphine as a method of pain relief and when I asked if it was harmful to the baby the doctor responded with, "If it did I would lose my license". I guess he should lose his license because that was the beginning of this nightmare. No actually, the beginning was when it was recommended by a hospital staff member that I stay home after my water broke.

Fast forward after 24 hours of labor, no doctor being available to deliver my baby leading to him having to be resuscitated (or maybe that was the morphine). During the following 3 days he was not properly evaluated to see if he could latch and if I was producing enough milk and so he was slowly losing weight but still "within normal limits". We were dismissed but after an awful night of him crying non-stop, shaking and essentially fighting for his life we went back to the hospital to learn that he WASN'T latching properly and I WASN'T producing enough milk. They weighed him before and after a feeding. He had lost 1 lb. since being born 3 days earlier.  SO HE WASN'T WITHIN NORMAL LIMITS but rather borderline high risk. He was monitored for 24 hours while drinking formula and thankfully was gaining weight, healthy and without any brain damage or other permanent consequences.

Well, the hospital decided to charge us the second time we were admitted for essentially doing their job the first time. We disputed our case and called at least once a month to follow-up making sure that they wouldn't send us to collections as written on their invoice. Well 1 year later with dozens of calls to this hospital, they DID send us to collections despite the fact they said they wouldn't and refused to reverse the charges. They did offer us a discount IF WE PAID IN FULL.

SHAME ON YOU!!!!!!! This is not a business of selling cars. HEALTHCARE IS NOT NEGOTIABLE AND ANY ONE WITH COMMON SENSE AND A HEART WOULD NOT TRY TO MAKE A PROFIT FROM THIS SITUATION.

I WILL NEVER GO TO MARIN GENERAL AGAIN. BE CAREFUL IF YOU DO. The person in charge in the financing department, WHICH I WILL REMAIN NAMELESS is not a good person. PERIOD.<//Review>

<UserId.>106662040948166721580</UserId.><user_name>Richard Pico<//user_name><Date>1444076959698< /Date><Rate>4</Rate><text>Time of visit was Monday, 100515, at approximately 1145, just before noon. Parked on Bryant, $2/Hr.

When I walked in there were 6 people at the bar. All tables were empty. Dressed in Raider black & silver, male bartender asked if I was eating lunch.

I ordered the grand slam burger, roll, with both cheeses, medium, and fries. Hamburger arrived on a platter containing a half avacado, grilled onions, two slices of pickles, one slice of tomato, and one leaf of romaine lettuce. This was a well presented platter, with the french fries & sandwich taking up most of the platter.

As I waited, two hose monsters stepped in taking a table to the rear. Their legs were big and shapely and very desirable.

My burger was deeeelicious. Juicy, moist and very flavorful is all I can say. Roll was soft, fresh, moist and wonderful. French fries were just right. The grilled onions were, too, just right.

This burger was one of the better burgers I have had in a while. They beat Gotts Roadside in Napa.

Why not five stars? Did not use lavatory. Bartender was very quiet, knowing full well I had not been in there in the past. He could have provided more conversation especially when he said Lincecum is coming back to the SF Giants next year. I guess I expect too much entertainment from a local bartender.

Finally, near the end of my gut splitting meal, a blond cross-dresser walked in wearing skin tight workout pants. If you don't mind me saying, but you have a fantastic derriere. What a way to end a fabulous meal.

Bar and kitchen open at 7 AM. Breakfast served 7 - 11 AM; kitchen closes at 2:30 PM.

Cloth napkins (red), by the way.

Coke + meal came to $17.67, a little steep, but better than Gotts Roadside Burger.

Double play is worth a second look.</text>< Pics>

I can only recommend one florist to anyone: Cindy's Flowers. I've attended two very exclusive, high end events in the past few months and the flowers at each were done by Cindy. They were  outstanding, genuinely breathtaking and lovelier than any flowers I've ever received or sent or seen, anywhere.

One event was a flower bar, where dozens and dozens of the company's clients were invited to select a large, generous bouquet of their choosing, without size limitations. There were dozens of exotic, unusual and beautiful flowers, branches, leaves, herbs, etc... to choose from; it was quite a sight! But it was a genuine and amazing experience to see each person stand in line, take in all that beauty, choose exactly what they most desired and then have this lovely woman add colors, textures and balance to each bouquet and make it Far more beautiful than they had imagined. The OOHS! Ahhhs! and omg's were like being at a great fireworks show. But more. Clusters of friends and colleagues stood nearby, to catch a glimpse of those eager, glowing faces of people feeling heard and appreciated in a whole new way. It was people watching at it's best; sharing in a common joy, a unique experience and experiencing real joy together. I've never seen anything like it, never understood the power of flowers and I'll never forget that experience.

Some people have an incredible eye for color, balance, use of space, fashion, design, etc... Cindy really found her calling as a florist of the highest caliber. Her large flower arrangements are genuinely breathtaking; having  a level of dimension where you see something more from every angle and as you get closer, it's like an entire wonderland of color, texture and balance. I cannot imagine having the talent and ability to create such beauty, even with a garden of my own, abundant with flowers.

Her work, her kindness, her empathy and generosity of spirit are just remarkable. It all translates into her work, to express all you entrust to her, to express the very best you wish for friends, family and colleagues.

This is the only place I'll recommend and go to for flowers. There just is no comparison.  I wanted to post some of the 30+ photos of the flowers at the event and they're gone. You'll just have to have a look for yourselves!</text>

< Text>
I wanted to send flowers to my cousin for her birthday 3/4/20 and looked up florists in Menlo Park, CA and found Cindy's Flowers. The website pictures looked nice and the prices seemed reasonable. I picked out Eau de Tulips, which is described as "Ten tulip stems, submerged under water, create a striking presentation for all to "sea" and enjoy" - See 3rd photo.  My cousin received a plain vase with tulips, none of which were submerged under water. In fact, it looked like any grocery store bunch of tulips stuck in a vase. Nothing special, although the tulips are very pretty. See 1st photo. Very disappointing when the online picture looked so stunning and unique.

I immediately emailed Cindy on 3/5/20 and explained what happened. I asked for a full refund or re-delivery of the product I paid for. She responded and said she would bring new flowers that day.

My cousin sent me a picture of what she got as the "replacement" flowers. See 2nd picture. The delivery person walked up and said "I hope you liked it. They did not look stunning or elegant or like anything I would have ordered.

CAUTION - go with another company. Or just get the simple flowers in a vase and get what you pay for.< /Text>

< review>
I attended very small class (of 3) and Eric was our instructor. He was right off the bat very friendly and welcoming. He was knowledgeable and answered every question clearly. I‚Äôve taken 2 other CPR classes before and was not as engaged as I was at Professional CPR because Eric kept our attention. The front desk person was super nice as well! The office is clean and they offer coffee, snacks and free WiFi!

I believe the class I was in was about 2.5 hours? I think the duration of the class depends on how big the class is. They tell you it‚Äôs about 3-4 hours because it can take up to that long.

There was a slide show presentation, a short video and then all the action begins! We practiced with an child/adult dummy and a baby dummy. After practicing there is a small test which is open book (you are required to have a book, which they offer for I think $17).
You receive your card VIA e-mail the same day so that‚Äôs pretty awesome!

Overall great experience! I would highly recommend them!</review>

< review>
I attended one of the Adult and Child CPR/AED and First Aid classes with ProCPR and it was the perfect, small classroom setting that I was looking for! Denae was my instructor and made sure to keep the 4 hour class as short, but informative as possible. There were only 8 students in my class, which went from about 6:30 to 10:30, but the amount of students made it really comfortable to ask questions and not be afraid to practice on the dummy. Overall, the class was incredibly thorough when it came to CPR and AED, but the First Aid portion was a little rushed through. Seeing as you can watch basic first aid videos online, I didn‚Äôt mind sticking to the most important parts of First Aid. The classroom was incredibly clean, nice, and there was a selection of snacks and coffee. I would definitely recommend ProCPR to anyone who needs to take a CPR or First Aid class and wants a comfortable, small class with very hands on instructors.<//review>
